URL pattern definition, URL matching/resolution, and URL reversing.\\n\\n### Core URL Pattern Definition (django/urls/conf.py)\\n\\nThe `django/urls/conf.py` module provides the public API for defining URL patterns:\\n\\n- **include()** - Function that allows including URL patterns from other modules or inline URL pattern lists. Returns a tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace)\\n- **path()** - Creates URL patterns using a simpler, more readable syntax (e.g., `path('articles/<int:year>/', view)`)\\n- **re_path()** - Creates URL patterns using regular expressions (e.g., `re_path(r'^articles/(?P<year>[0-9]{4})/$', view)`)\\n- **_path()** - Internal helper function that both path() and re_path() are based on via functools.partial, handling the common logic for creating URL patterns\\n\\n### URL Dispatcher and Resolution (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n\\nThis module contains the core URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions:\\n\\n**Pattern Classes:**\\n- **RegexPattern** - Handles regex-based URL patterns with full regex capabilities\\n- **RoutePattern** - Handles simplified path() patterns using angle bracket syntax like `<int:pk>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** - Special pattern for internationalized URLs, used by i18n_patterns()\\n\\n**Main Classes:**\\n- **URLPattern** - Represents a single URL pattern that maps to a view. Contains pattern, callback, default_args, and name\\n- **URLResolver** - Represents a resolver that can contain nested URL patterns. Acts as a container for both URLPattern and nested URLResolver instances\\n- **ResolverMatch** - Returned from successful URL resolution, contains the matched view function, captured arguments, kwargs, url_name, and namespace information\\n\\n**Key Functions:**\\n- **get_resolver()** - Returns a URLResolver instance for the given URLconf, with caching via _get_cached_resolver()\\n- **_route_to_regex()** - Converts simplified path() routes to compiled regular expressions and extracts converters (e.g., `<int:id>` becomes `(?P<id>[0-9]+)`)\\n- **URLResolver.resolve()** - Main URL resolution method that takes a path string and returns a ResolverMatch or raises Resolver404\\n- **URLResolver._populate()** - Populates internal lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution and caching\\n\\n### URL Resolution and Reversal (django/urls/base.py)\\n\\nThis module provides the high-level URL resolution and reversal API:\\n\\n- **resolve()** - Takes a URL path and returns a ResolverMatch by calling get_resolver(urlconf).resolve(path)\\n- **reverse()** - Takes a view name and returns the corresponding URL, with support for namespaces, args, kwargs, query parameters, and fragments\\n- **reverse_lazy()** - Lazy version of reverse() for use at module load time\\n- **get_urlconf()** - Returns the currently active URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task\\n- **set_urlconf()** - Sets a custom URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task (useful in tests and middleware)\\n- **is_valid_path()** - Convenience wrapper that returns a ResolverMatch if path resolves, False otherwise\\n- **translate_url()** - Translates URLs between languages using i18n_patterns\\n\\n### URL Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\n\\nProvides type converters for path() parameters:\\n\\n- **IntConverter** - Matches integers in URLs\\n- **StringConverter** - Matches any string except '/'\\n- **UUIDConverter** - Matches UUID format strings\\n- **SlugConverter** - Matches slug format (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores)\\n- **PathConverter** - Matches any string including '/'\\n- **get_converters()** - Returns dict of all available converters (built-in + registered)\\n- **register_converter()** - Allows applications to register custom converters\\n\\n### Exceptions (django/urls/exceptions.py)\\n\\n- **Resolver404** - Raised when a URL path cannot be resolved to a view (subclass of Http404)\\n- **NoReverseMatch** - Raised when reverse() cannot find a URL for the given view name\\n\\n### Utilities (django/urls/utils.py)\\n\\n- **get_callable()** - Converts string import paths like 'myapp.views.myview' to actual callable view functions\\n- **get_mod_func()** - Splits a dotted path into module and function name\\n\\n### Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\n\\n- **i18n_patterns()** - Wraps URL patterns to add language code prefixes (e.g., '/en/', '/fr/')\\n- **is_language_prefix_patterns_used()** - Detects if i18n_patterns is used in the URLconf\\n\\n### Static Files (django/conf/urls/static.py)\\n\\n- **static()** - Helper function to serve static files in development mode using a URL pattern\\n\\n### Configuration (django/conf/urls/__init__.py)\\n\\nExports handler error views (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500) and the include() function for backwards compatibility.\\n\\n### Migration from patterns() to list (Django 1.10)\\n\\nThe **patterns()** function from `django.conf.urls` was removed in Django 1.10. Prior to 1.10, URL patterns were defined using:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.conf.urls import patterns, url\\nurlpatterns = patterns('myapp.views', \\n    url(r'^article/$', 'article_view'),\\n)\\n```\\n\\nModern Django (1.10+) uses direct list syntax with path() and re_path():\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.urls import path, re_path\\nfrom . import views\\nurlpatterns = [\\n    path('article/', views.article_view),\\n    re_path(r'^regex/(?P<id>[0-9]+)/$', views.view_with_id),\\n]\\n```\\n\\nThe URL dispatcher's URLResolver and URLPattern classes handle both the old string-based view references (via get_callable()) and modern callable/class-based views, providing backwards compatibility during the transition period.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":836,"cache_read_input_tokens":85810,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":836},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"65e95dd3-1a24-4f74-91a7-5874601b469c","uuid":"3ca6933b-0d2c-4c25-972f-c203d154b816"}

core modules that handle URL pattern definition, URL matching/resolution, and URL reversing.\\n\\n### Core URL Pattern Definition (django/urls/conf.py)\\n\\nThe `django/urls/conf.py` module provides the public API for defining URL patterns:\\n\\n- **include()** - Function that allows including URL patterns from other modules or inline URL pattern lists. Returns a tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace)\\n- **path()** - Creates URL patterns using a simpler, more readable syntax (e.g., `path('articles/<int:year>/', view)`)\\n- **re_path()** - Creates URL patterns using regular expressions (e.g., `re_path(r'^articles/(?P<year>[0-9]{4})/$', view)`)\\n- **_path()** - Internal helper function that both path() and re_path() are based on via functools.partial, handling the common logic for creating URL patterns\\n\\n### URL Dispatcher and Resolution (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n\\nThis module contains the core URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions:\\n\\n**Pattern Classes:**\\n- **RegexPattern** - Handles regex-based URL patterns with full regex capabilities\\n- **RoutePattern** - Handles simplified path() patterns using angle bracket syntax like `<int:pk>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** - Special pattern for internationalized URLs, used by i18n_patterns()\\n\\n**Main Classes:**\\n- **URLPattern** - Represents a single URL pattern that maps to a view. Contains pattern, callback, default_args, and name\\n- **URLResolver** - Represents a resolver that can contain nested URL patterns. Acts as a container for both URLPattern and nested URLResolver instances\\n- **ResolverMatch** - Returned from successful URL resolution, contains the matched view function, captured arguments, kwargs, url_name, and namespace information\\n\\n**Key Functions:**\\n- **get_resolver()** - Returns a URLResolver instance for the given URLconf, with caching via _get_cached_resolver()\\n- **_route_to_regex()** - Converts simplified path() routes to compiled regular expressions and extracts converters (e.g., `<int:id>` becomes `(?P<id>[0-9]+)`)\\n- **URLResolver.resolve()** - Main URL resolution method that takes a path string and returns a ResolverMatch or raises Resolver404\\n- **URLResolver._populate()** - Populates internal lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution and caching\\n\\n### URL Resolution and Reversal (django/urls/base.py)\\n\\nThis module provides the high-level URL resolution and reversal API:\\n\\n- **resolve()** - Takes a URL path and returns a ResolverMatch by calling get_resolver(urlconf).resolve(path)\\n- **reverse()** - Takes a view name and returns the corresponding URL, with support for namespaces, args, kwargs, query parameters, and fragments\\n- **reverse_lazy()** - Lazy version of reverse() for use at module load time\\n- **get_urlconf()** - Returns the currently active URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task\\n- **set_urlconf()** - Sets a custom URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task (useful in tests and middleware)\\n- **is_valid_path()** - Convenience wrapper that returns a ResolverMatch if path resolves, False otherwise\\n- **translate_url()** - Translates URLs between languages using i18n_patterns\\n\\n### URL Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\n\\nProvides type converters for path() parameters:\\n\\n- **IntConverter** - Matches integers in URLs\\n- **StringConverter** - Matches any string except '/'\\n- **UUIDConverter** - Matches UUID format strings\\n- **SlugConverter** - Matches slug format (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores)\\n- **PathConverter** - Matches any string including '/'\\n- **get_converters()** - Returns dict of all available converters (built-in + registered)\\n- **register_converter()** - Allows applications to register custom converters\\n\\n### Exceptions (django/urls/exceptions.py)\\n\\n- **Resolver404** - Raised when a URL path cannot be resolved to a view (subclass of Http404)\\n- **NoReverseMatch** - Raised when reverse() cannot find a URL for the given view name\\n\\n### Utilities (django/urls/utils.py)\\n\\n- **get_callable()** - Converts string import paths like 'myapp.views.myview' to actual callable view functions\\n- **get_mod_func()** - Splits a dotted path into module and function name\\n\\n### Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\n\\n- **i18n_patterns()** - Wraps URL patterns to add language code prefixes (e.g., '/en/', '/fr/')\\n- **is_language_prefix_patterns_used()** - Detects if i18n_patterns is used in the URLconf\\n\\n### Static Files (django/conf/urls/static.py)\\n\\n- **static()** - Helper function to serve static files in development mode using a URL pattern\\n\\n### Configuration (django/conf/urls/__init__.py)\\n\\nExports handler error views (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500) and the include() function for backwards compatibility.\\n\\n### Migration from patterns() to list (Django 1.10)\\n\\nThe **patterns()** function from `django.conf.urls` was removed in Django 1.10. Prior to 1.10, URL patterns were defined using:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.conf.urls import patterns, url\\nurlpatterns = patterns('myapp.views', \\n    url(r'^article/$', 'article_view'),\\n)\\n```\\n\\nModern Django (1.10+) uses direct list syntax with path() and re_path():\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.urls import path, re_path\\nfrom . import views\\nurlpatterns = [\\n    path('article/', views.article_view),\\n    re_path(r'^regex/(?P<id>[0-9]+)/$', views.view_with_id),\\n]\\n```\\n\\nThe URL dispatcher's URLResolver and URLPattern classes handle both the old string-based view references (via get_callable()) and modern callable/class-based views, providing backwards compatibility during the transition period.\"\n    53→}\n    54→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. defining URL patterns:\\n\\n- **include()** - Function that allows including URL patterns from other modules or inline URL pattern lists. Returns a tuple of (urlconf_module, app_name, namespace)\\n- **path()** - Creates URL patterns using a simpler, more readable syntax (e.g., `path('articles/<int:year>/', view)`)\\n- **re_path()** - Creates URL patterns using regular expressions (e.g., `re_path(r'^articles/(?P<year>[0-9]{4})/$', view)`)\\n- **_path()** - Internal helper function that both path() and re_path() are based on via functools.partial, handling the common logic for creating URL patterns\\n\\n### URL Dispatcher and Resolution (django/urls/resolvers.py)\\n\\nThis module contains the core URL dispatcher that processes both legacy and current URL definitions:\\n\\n**Pattern Classes:**\\n- **RegexPattern** - Handles regex-based URL patterns with full regex capabilities\\n- **RoutePattern** - Handles simplified path() patterns using angle bracket syntax like `<int:pk>`\\n- **LocalePrefixPattern** - Special pattern for internationalized URLs, used by i18n_patterns()\\n\\n**Main Classes:**\\n- **URLPattern** - Represents a single URL pattern that maps to a view. Contains pattern, callback, default_args, and name\\n- **URLResolver** - Represents a resolver that can contain nested URL patterns. Acts as a container for both URLPattern and nested URLResolver instances\\n- **ResolverMatch** - Returned from successful URL resolution, contains the matched view function, captured arguments, kwargs, url_name, and namespace information\\n\\n**Key Functions:**\\n- **get_resolver()** - Returns a URLResolver instance for the given URLconf, with caching via _get_cached_resolver()\\n- **_route_to_regex()** - Converts simplified path() routes to compiled regular expressions and extracts converters (e.g., `<int:id>` becomes `(?P<id>[0-9]+)`)\\n- **URLResolver.resolve()** - Main URL resolution method that takes a path string and returns a ResolverMatch or raises Resolver404\\n- **URLResolver._populate()** - Populates internal lookup dictionaries for reverse URL resolution and caching\\n\\n### URL Resolution and Reversal (django/urls/base.py)\\n\\nThis module provides the high-level URL resolution and reversal API:\\n\\n- **resolve()** - Takes a URL path and returns a ResolverMatch by calling get_resolver(urlconf).resolve(path)\\n- **reverse()** - Takes a view name and returns the corresponding URL, with support for namespaces, args, kwargs, query parameters, and fragments\\n- **reverse_lazy()** - Lazy version of reverse() for use at module load time\\n- **get_urlconf()** - Returns the currently active URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task\\n- **set_urlconf()** - Sets a custom URLconf for the current thread/asyncio task (useful in tests and middleware)\\n- **is_valid_path()** - Convenience wrapper that returns a ResolverMatch if path resolves, False otherwise\\n- **translate_url()** - Translates URLs between languages using i18n_patterns\\n\\n### URL Converters (django/urls/converters.py)\\n\\nProvides type converters for path() parameters:\\n\\n- **IntConverter** - Matches integers in URLs\\n- **StringConverter** - Matches any string except '/'\\n- **UUIDConverter** - Matches UUID format strings\\n- **SlugConverter** - Matches slug format (letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores)\\n- **PathConverter** - Matches any string including '/'\\n- **get_converters()** - Returns dict of all available converters (built-in + registered)\\n- **register_converter()** - Allows applications to register custom converters\\n\\n### Exceptions (django/urls/exceptions.py)\\n\\n- **Resolver404** - Raised when a URL path cannot be resolved to a view (subclass of Http404)\\n- **NoReverseMatch** - Raised when reverse() cannot find a URL for the given view name\\n\\n### Utilities (django/urls/utils.py)\\n\\n- **get_callable()** - Converts string import paths like 'myapp.views.myview' to actual callable view functions\\n- **get_mod_func()** - Splits a dotted path into module and function name\\n\\n### Internationalization (django/conf/urls/i18n.py)\\n\\n- **i18n_patterns()** - Wraps URL patterns to add language code prefixes (e.g., '/en/', '/fr/')\\n- **is_language_prefix_patterns_used()** - Detects if i18n_patterns is used in the URLconf\\n\\n### Static Files (django/conf/urls/static.py)\\n\\n- **static()** - Helper function to serve static files in development mode using a URL pattern\\n\\n### Configuration (django/conf/urls/__init__.py)\\n\\nExports handler error views (handler400, handler403, handler404, handler500) and the include() function for backwards compatibility.\\n\\n### Migration from patterns() to list (Django 1.10)\\n\\nThe **patterns()** function from `django.conf.urls` was removed in Django 1.10. Prior to 1.10, URL patterns were defined using:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.conf.urls import patterns, url\\nurlpatterns = patterns('myapp.views', \\n    url(r'^article/$', 'article_view'),\\n)\\n```\\n\\nModern Django (1.10+) uses direct list syntax with path() and re_path():\\n\\n```python\\nfrom django.urls import path, re_path\\nfrom . import views\\nurlpatterns = [\\n    path('article/', views.article_view),\\n    re_path(r'^regex/(?P<id>[0-9]+)/$', views.view_with_id),\\n]\\n```\\n\\nThe URL dispatcher's URLResolver and URLPattern classes handle both the old string-based view references (via get_callable()) and modern callable/class-based views, providing backwards compatibility during the transition period.\"\n}\n","numLines":54,"startLine":1,"totalLines":54}}}
